# Skills Index

Consult only the skill document relevant to the current task. If no specific skill applies,
refer to `AGENTS.md` and `.mustflow/config/commands.toml` to implement the most minimal safe change.

## Selection Rules

- At task start and before the first edit, compare the user request and expected changed files with
  the triggers below.
- If one or more triggers match, read each `SKILL.md` before editing that scope.
- When a skill is used, or when a plausible skill is intentionally skipped, leave a concise
  selection note in the next user-facing update or final report.
- If a new condition appears during the task, such as a command failure, test contract change, or
  documentation change, pause and read the newly matching skill before continuing.
- If no trigger applies, do not invent a skill. Continue with `AGENTS.md`,
  `.mustflow/docs/agent-workflow.md`, and `.mustflow/config/commands.toml`.
- Skill documents guide procedure only. They do not authorize command execution outside the declared
  command intents.
- Keep the route table compact: each route states the trigger, required input, edit scope, risk,
  verification intents, and expected output.
- Keep `.mustflow/skills/routes.toml` aligned with the route table when adding, removing, or
  reclassifying skill routes. The TOML metadata supports strict validation of route category,
  route type, priority, and mutually exclusive route references.
- When a current `mf classify` report or changed-file validation reason list is already available,
  use it only as a prefilter before scanning the route table. Do not run a new command solely to
  select skills unless the command contract already authorizes that command.

## Selection Convention

- Choose one main route: a `primary` route for ordinary work or an `authoring` route for
  mustflow authoring and maintenance work. Prefer the most specific matching skill over a broad
  architecture or review skill.
- Treat `authoring` routes as selectable main routes, not adjunct routes. Use them when the task
  creates or maintains mustflow-owned skills, context files, command contracts, route metadata, or
  public documentation entries.
- Add no more than two adjunct skills for secondary risks such as tests, documentation, security,
  privacy, release, or contract drift.
- Use `completion-evidence-gate` as a final reporting adjunct when a completion, readiness, merge,
  release, install, or verification claim needs current repository evidence.
- Use `complex-decision-analysis` as a primary route only when analysis or a decision record is the
  current deliverable, the task has both a material uncertainty signal and a material consequence
  signal, and no narrower primary route owns the complete problem. Before implementation, switch to
  the narrowest matching implementation skill.
- Use `automation-investment-case-review` as a primary route when deciding whether an AI agent,
  workflow automation, internal tool, or integration is worth building, expanding, replacing, or
  retiring from accepted-outcome cost, human comparison, supervision, failure recovery,
  maintenance, break-even, throughput value, effective lifetime, NPV, and independent safety gates.
- Use `product-onboarding-activation-review` as a primary route when account-first versus pre-account
  core value, signup checkpoints, guest-to-account transfer, authentication choices, first-run
  questions, personalization, editable samples, contextual help, tutorial depth, progressive
  disclosure, or a focused primary action must improve a user-owned activation result, retained use,
  or paid conversion without excluding account or onboarding abandoners from the denominator.
- Use `subscription-retention-profit-review` as a primary route when cancellation reasons, save
  offers, downgrade, pause, credits, discounts, dormant-user reactivation, win-back, offer ordering,
  or retained-value claims must be decided from holdout-backed incremental contribution rather than
  offer acceptance, natural return, or paused-user counts.
- Use `product-engagement-retention-review` as a primary route when weekly value reports, saved-time
  summaries, artifact recaps, streaks, grace or recovery, attendance rewards, abandoned-work
  reminders, or notification timing must improve completed value and retained use without counting
  activity theater, reward claims, natural return, or message opens as durable retention.
- Use `credit-monetization-integrity-review` as a primary route when credit-offer timing, discount
  versus bonus framing, pack count or spacing, purchased-credit expiry, subscription rollover,
  balance-class rights, spend order, or exact or bounded pre-execution pricing must improve
  long-horizon contribution without deceptive equivalence, breakage theater, or surprise deductions.
- Use `pricing-model-integrity-review` as a primary route when trial card collection, lifetime or
  founder access, local currency, regional pricing, subscription versus usage or hybrid pricing,
  price elasticity, annual prepay, or annual discounts must improve eligible-cohort contribution
  without hidden renewal, unbounded future-cost rights, or cash-revenue confusion.
- Use `game-economy-monetization-review` as a primary route when paid or rewarded-ad revives, lives,
  energy, refills, unlimited play, VIP benefits, IAP cannibalization, or content pacing must improve
  long-horizon player contribution without selling ranked outcomes or erasing meaningful failure.
- Use `freemium-ad-monetization-review` as a primary route when free-tier limits, ad-supported access,
  interstitial or rewarded-ad placement, first-value suppression, premium ad removal, or ad
  frequency must improve contribution without interrupting active work or holding results hostage.
- Use `referral-incentive-integrity-review` as a primary route when inviter, invitee, dual-sided, or
  tiered referral rewards, attribution, valid-referral qualification, vesting, reversal, self-referral,
  reward farming, or incremental referral contribution is created, changed, reviewed, or reported.
- Use `llm-product-monetization-review` as a primary route when token versus task pricing, bounded AI
  work units, standard versus precision tiers, free versus paid queue priority, automatic failure
  restoration or retry rights, model disclosure or pinning, managed provider cost, BYOK, customer API
  keys, platform fees, or LLM failed-work charging changes.
- Use `game-liveops-commerce-integrity-review` as a primary route when season passes, memberships,
  liveops cadence, cosmetics, power goods, deterministic bundles, loot boxes, odds, pity, payer
  concentration, or game commerce production and fairness risk changes.
- Use `growth-distribution-integrity-review` as a primary route when result watermarking, embedded
  attribution, affiliate or influencer compensation, recurring commission, partner attribution,
  owned-product cross-promotion, portfolio fatigue, brand confusion, or incremental distribution
  contribution changes.
- Use `product-portfolio-integrity-review` as a primary route when unified accounts, shared credit
  wallets, individual versus bundled subscriptions, portfolio entitlements, umbrella or endorsed
  brands, cross-product reuse, cannibalization, or failure spillover changes.
- Use `localization-market-expansion-review` as a primary route when first-market language,
  simultaneous versus staged locale rollout, AI translation review depth, exploratory versus
  revenue-ready locales, localized SEO demand, or per-locale retained contribution changes.
- Use `desktop-commercial-distribution-review` as a primary route when a desktop product compares
  website delivery with Microsoft Store, Mac App Store, or hybrid distribution across commerce,
  licensing, trust, capabilities, updates, fees, conversion, and retained contribution.
- Use `client-platform-strategy-review` as a primary route when a product compares web-first,
  PWA, cross-platform, or native clients, calculates native break-even, or chooses local-first,
  cloud-first, offline, sync, privacy, and recovery authority.
- Use `service-portfolio-capital-allocation-review` as a primary route when shared backend investment,
  correlated failure cells, service continuation or shutdown, rescue experiments, or founder time
  between new launches and existing-product improvements changes.
- Use `technology-stack-selection` as the narrower primary route when the decision chooses,
  adopts, replaces, rejects, or standardizes a technology stack, vendor, framework, database,
  queue, auth, payment, AI provider, hosting, deployment, build, ORM, or observability surface.
  Treat it as the survival-path gate before broader decision analysis when migration, rollback,
  maintainer capacity, debugging surface, CI/CD, deployment cost, or long-term operations are the
  deciding factors.
- Use `proactive-risk-surfacing` as an event route when current evidence reveals a scope-adjacent
  risk outside the literal request and the agent must decide whether to fix now, report only, ask
  first, or ignore it without broadening into unrelated work.
- Use `ai-generated-code-hardening` as an adjunct when assistant-authored, AI-generated, or
  broad code changes need a repository-evidence pass for symptom-only fixes, pinpoint
  hardcoding, same-defect-class siblings, duplicate helpers or shapes, hidden coupling,
  public-surface drift, swallowed errors, excessive complexity, and weak tests.
- Use `ai-product-readiness-review` as a primary route when an AI product feature, AI Gateway,
  provider/model integration, prompt/RAG/tool path, AI cache, fallback path, streaming path,
  eval gate, user-data flow, model registry, observability surface, or model portability plan
  needs end-to-end product readiness review before narrower prompt, cost, latency, agent,
  privacy, cache, or UX skills take over.
- Use `prompt-contract-quality-review` as a primary route when prompts, prompt builders,
  RAG assembly, structured outputs, tool-use instructions, model settings, eval fixtures,
  refusal states, or agent completion definitions need prompt-as-function review for
  input contracts, authority separation, output schemas, fallback states, and eval evidence.
- Use `llm-hallucination-control-review` as a primary route when LLM answers, RAG responses,
  citations, claim maps, evidence IDs, answerability states, retrieval thresholds, validators,
  abstain behavior, or hallucination metrics need product-controlled grounding review.
- Use `llm-token-cost-control-review` as a primary route when LLM request assembly, token budgets,
  prompt caching, chat history, RAG context size, prompt packing, document metadata, source maps,
  question-scoped compression, evidence cards, tool or schema payloads, model routing, reasoning
  budget, retries, Batch, Flex, predicted outputs, or cost-per-success telemetry need token spend
  review.
- Use `llm-response-latency-review` as a primary route when LLM response speed, time to first
  token, first useful output, streaming, output length, LLM round trips, tool wait, prompt-cache
  latency, model routing speed, speculative or parallel work, realtime continuation, priority
  tiers, or predicted outputs need latency review.
- Use `llm-model-routing-integrity-review` as a primary route when model selection, small-to-large
  cascades, escalation, fallback, stage switching, verifier thresholds, context-handoff loss,
  distribution shift, or OOD behavior must preserve accepted outcomes while minimizing total route,
  verification, repair, latency, and operating cost.
- Use `agent-execution-control-review` as a primary route when autonomous or semi-autonomous LLM
  agents, agentic workflows, planners, executors, verifiers, tool contracts, tool-call gates,
  risk-tiered approval or interrupt flows, reversibility, external effects, durable agent state,
  handoffs, guardrails, loop budgets, retry classification, trace evaluation, or outcome metrics
  need execution-control review.
- Use `agent-planning-recovery-review` as a primary route when a long-running agent needs a stable
  global goal and dependency graph, short rolling plans, event-triggered replanning, append-only
  state, rebuildable snapshots and prompt views, deterministic replay, or effect identity across
  interruptions and replans.
- Use `agent-release-bundle-rollout-review` as a primary route when models, rendered prompts, tools,
  policies, retrieval, memory, runtimes, and evaluators must form one immutable agent behavior
  bundle promoted through offline replay, effect-free shadowing, sticky canaries, staged expansion,
  hard safety gates, compatibility, rollback, and attenuation-only emergency restriction.
- Use `agent-runtime-multi-worker-review` as a primary route when a production agent runtime must
  decide whether independent parallel work justifies several agents, then define orchestrator-worker
  topology, specialized roles, artifact ownership, correlation controls, bounded fan-out, and one
  central verifier.
- Use `agent-runtime-isolation-review` as a primary route when durable agent state must outlive
  short-lived queued workers, model-directed shell, browser, file, package, or code work needs an
  ephemeral sandbox, credentials must be temporary and task-scoped, or production effects need a
  trusted policy broker outside the sandbox.
- Use `agent-memory-context-governance-review` as a primary route when persistent user or project
  memory, conversation history, memory extraction or consolidation, summaries, structured task
  state, long-context assembly, retrieval admission, supersession, expiry, deletion, privacy, or
  memory quality needs scope, provenance, freshness, authority, and lifecycle review.
- Use `browser-automation-reliability-review` as a primary route when browser automation,
  UI automation, Playwright, Selenium, Puppeteer, WebDriver, browser-driving agents, flaky
  selectors, page readiness, auth state, CAPTCHA or anti-bot handling, rate limits, screenshot
  verification, retry, timeout, human approval, or browser automation observability needs
  reliability review before narrower agent, auth, API, frontend, or test-suite skills take over.
- Use `agent-eval-integrity-review` as a primary route when agent evaluation loops, trace or
  trajectory grading, LLM judges, outcome scoring, eval datasets, golden or dirty sets, pass@k or
  pass^k metrics, shadow environments, production-monitoring-to-eval feedback, or agent regression
  gates need final-state and trajectory evidence rather than judge-model opinion.
- Use `abstraction-boundary-review` as an adjunct when implementation or review needs to decide
  whether a helper, interface, adapter, service, policy object, strategy, mapper, DTO, base class,
  component, or shared module should exist by comparing reason-to-change, public promise, ownership,
  layer import contracts, side-effect placement, interface necessity, boilerplate deletion, test
  shape, reversibility, deduplication safety, post-refactor layer integrity, and over- or
  under-abstraction signals.
- Use `module-boundary-review` as an adjunct when module separation needs change-spread, data-owner,
  change-axis, stability-direction, policy-owner, failure-owner, import-direction, DTO leakage,
  shared-helper, public-API, shallow-module, or caller sequencing review before deciding whether a
  boundary is real.
- Use `split-refactor-residual-path-review` as an adjunct when a split or extraction claims a
  handler, listener, state mutation, event processor, side effect, or cleanup responsibility moved
  and the review must prove the old file or fallback path cannot still process the same event.
- Use `change-blast-radius-review` as an adjunct when maintainability review needs to predict the
  next-change spread, feature deletion path, policy owner, workflow owner, config or tenant branch
  spread, event contract visibility, migration/runtime compatibility, or whether a clean-looking
  abstraction actually lowers future edit cost.
- Use `business-rule-leakage-review` as an adjunct when money, permission, ownership, state,
  settlement, discount, inventory, notification, subscription, visibility, eligibility, report, or
  tenant rules may be enforced in only one UI, controller, query, mapper, batch, webhook, cache,
  admin tool, support path, or report instead of a shared rule owner.
- Use `small-service-platform-architecture-review` as a primary route when a multi-product
  platform, app factory, shared account portal, Product Registry, entitlement and credit platform,
  deployment factory, analytics spine, common UI, template system, or operations automation must
  support many small product apps before specialist auth, payment, admin, notification,
  localization, deployment, AI, file, queue, or service-boundary skills take over.
- Use `payment-integrity-review` as an adjunct when payment, checkout, authorization, capture,
  refund, subscription, provider webhook, fulfillment, entitlement, ledger, coupon, inventory,
  settlement, dispute, chargeback, or payment-provider integration code needs money-event integrity
  review for idempotency, ordering, ownership, amount, currency, retry, reconciliation, or audit
  risk.
- Use `credit-ledger-integrity-review` as an adjunct when credits, points, wallet balances, reward
  points, prepaid or usage credits, purchased versus subscription or promotional balance classes,
  balance deductions, accruals, refunds, expirations, rollovers, user-visible price quotes,
  reservations, captures, releases, admin adjustments, ledger tables, balance caches, or
  reconciliation jobs need ledger integrity review for idempotency, atomic balance changes,
  concurrency, ordering, ownership, amount precision, policy snapshots, quote binding, expiry lots,
  audit, or reconciliation risk.
- Use `dual-write-consistency` as an adjunct when one logical operation commits local state and
  separately publishes, projects, calls, or writes another independently committed system, so
  crash points, outbox or inbox delivery, reconciliation, and eventual convergence must be proved.
- Use `durable-workflow-orchestration` as a primary route when one business outcome spans multiple
  persisted commands, entities, services, callbacks, timers, approvals, retries, or compensations
  and must resume safely after process loss or deployment.
- Use `execution-ledger-integrity-review` as an adjunct when runs, attempts, leases, approvals,
  checkpoints, effects, receipts, terminal outcomes, reconciliation, or replay need append-only
  execution truth rather than logs or session summaries.
- Use `policy-decision-integrity-review` as an adjunct when a versioned policy, specification,
  decision table, capability, approval rule, limit, or masking rule derives allow, deny,
  require-approval, downgrade, or obligations from actor, resource, action, context, and budget.
- Use `structured-concurrency-supervision-review` as an adjunct when one runtime parent starts
  concurrent children and correctness depends on bounded fan-out, ownership, deadline and
  cancellation propagation, joining, sibling failure policy, cleanup, or rejecting late results.
- Use `notification-delivery-integrity-review` as an adjunct when notification generation, email,
  push, SMS, in-app inboxes, unsubscribe, suppression, digest, quiet hours, timezone scheduling,
  provider webhooks, delivery attempts, templates, or notification audit logs need delivery
  lifecycle review across source events, intents, schedules, channels, provider outcomes, consent,
  dedupe, retry, and explainability.
- Use `api-misuse-resistance-review` as an adjunct when APIs, SDKs, service methods, DTOs, request
  shapes, response shapes, pagination, idempotency, async jobs, versioning, deprecation, rate
  limits, retry rules, observability, or caller-facing docs need caller-ergonomics and misuse-risk
  review rather than only schema compatibility.
- Use `third-party-api-integration-review` as an adjunct when a third-party SDK or external API
  integration needs production-readiness review for auth scopes, sandbox/production separation,
  timeouts, retries, rate limits, idempotency, pagination, webhooks, provider error mapping,
  SDK/API version drift, changelogs, migration guides, observability, or failure-path tests.
- Use `http-api-semantics-review` as an adjunct when HTTP method choices, safe/idempotent/cacheable
  claims, GET/HEAD bodies, OPTIONS or Allow discovery, HTTP QUERY, POST versus PUT URI ownership,
  PUT replacement, PATCH document formats, DELETE behavior, conditional requests, status codes,
  cache headers, CORS method discovery, retry behavior, or intermediary compatibility need HTTP
  semantics review rather than only schema compatibility.
- Use `api-access-control-review` as an adjunct when API security review needs BOLA or IDOR,
  object, property, or function authorization, tenant isolation, request-supplied identity,
  mass assignment, signed URLs, queue revalidation, webhook ownership, token/session hardening,
  account enumeration, automation defense, or denial-case coverage.
- Use `admin-control-plane-safety-review` as an adjunct when admin panels, backoffice tools,
  support consoles, operator dashboards, staff APIs, audit logs, change history, impersonation,
  dangerous actions, approvals, exports, imports, bulk operations, admin search or filters,
  production guardrails, PII masking, admin sessions, or MFA need control-plane safety review.
- Use `file-upload-security-review` as an adjunct when file uploads, imports, attachments,
  direct-to-storage uploads, remote file fetches, archive extraction, previews, thumbnails,
  conversions, scanner gates, immutable object versions, decoded-media budgets, storage keys,
  signed URLs, downloads, browser headers, or uploaded filename display need full file-lifecycle
  security review.
- Use `error-message-integrity-review` as an adjunct when error messages, codes, logs, validation
  failures, parse failures, public/internal error mapping, provider errors, retryability, support
  IDs, structured diagnostics, redaction, or troubleshooting text need recoverability and evidence
  review rather than prose polishing.
- Use `memory-lifetime-review` as an adjunct when code creates, registers, caches, spawns, opens,
  subscribes, schedules, streams, or otherwise retains values or resources whose cleanup,
  cancellation, eviction, shutdown, or ownership transfer must be reviewed.
- Use `desktop-memory-footprint-review` as an adjunct when Windows, macOS, Linux, Electron,
  WebView, WPF, WinUI, Win32, Qt, Java Swing or JavaFX, .NET, JVM, Rust, C++, Python, or other
  desktop app code needs scenario-level memory review across working set versus private memory,
  RSS, dirty pages, live set, peak and after-close memory, UI and data virtualization, renderer and
  window count, module loading, image decode size, OS-discardable caches, memory-mapped files,
  pooled buffers, native handles, detached UI trees, duplicate strings, large buffer capacity,
  object graph shape, undo history, inactive views, low-memory signals, and memory budgets.
- Use `hot-path-performance-review` as an adjunct when code review needs a cheap count of repeated
  ordinary work, boundary crossings, copy or allocation churn, wait points, and lock or pool pressure
  before a broader performance-budget or measurement pass.
- Use `api-request-performance-review` as an adjunct when API endpoints, handlers, controllers,
  resolvers, serializers, mappers, service methods, or route-level request paths need
  per-request latency review for I/O counts, DB/ORM/Redis/external-call fan-out,
  pagination/count/index fit, transactions, pool wait, cache miss paths, serialization, response
  size, request-path CPU, or trace/span observability rather than only general hot-path repetition.
- Use `api-failure-triage` as a primary route when an API failure, SDK failure, browser request
  failure, CORS preflight, gateway/CDN/proxy issue, wrong status/body, auth failure, retry, rate
  limit, cache, OpenAPI drift, or deployment-config difference is not yet localized to one boundary.
- Use `auth-flow-triage` as a primary route when login, OAuth, OIDC, cookie, session, token,
  passkey, MFA, refresh, logout, or authorization-after-login failure is not yet localized to the
  identity, browser, provider, proxy, token, session-store, clock, rate-limit, or permission boundary.
- Use `docker-runtime-triage` as a primary route when Docker daemon, context, Compose, container
  start, crash loop, health, image pull, port, DNS, network, volume, storage, cgroup, OOM, signal,
  registry, or runtime failure is not yet localized to host, daemon, image, app, network, storage,
  resource, or registry boundaries.
- Use `ci-pipeline-triage` as a primary route when CI/CD workflow, pipeline, job, runner, trigger,
  cache, artifact, runner-minute billing, artifact storage or retention, deployment job, required
  check, or post-deploy verification failure or cost is not yet localized to trigger, runner,
  environment, build, test, cache, artifact, billing, deploy, or verification.
- Use `web-render-performance-review` as an adjunct when web frontend routes need first-render,
  Core Web Vitals, LCP, CLS, FCP, TTFB, critical CSS, font, image, iframe, third-party script,
  hydration, first-view data, resource-hint, CDN/cache, route-prefetch, or long-task review.
- Use `core-web-vitals-field-review` as an adjunct when Core Web Vitals needs field-data,
  RUM, CrUX, Search Console, Lighthouse-versus-field, LCP/INP/CLS percentile, LoAF,
  bfcache, speculation-rules, third-party, tag-manager, or release-regression review.
- Use `image-delivery-performance-review` as an adjunct when web image review needs LCP image
  discovery, responsive candidate selection, preload and priority hints, intrinsic dimensions,
  image formats and quality budgets, CDN transformation cache keys, `Accept` negotiation,
  metadata handling, SVG safety, or image optimizer abuse controls.
- Use `client-bundle-pruning-review` as an adjunct when frontend code review needs to reduce
  initial JS or shared vendor weight by fixing tree-shaking blockers, package entrypoints,
  barrels, side-effect metadata, client boundaries, dynamic imports, polyfills, browser targets,
  chunk rules, utility CSS extraction, or inline asset rules.
- Use `frame-render-performance-review` as an adjunct when frontend code review needs to reduce
  per-frame browser work, INP delay, scroll or animation jank, style recalculation, layout, paint,
  compositing, DOM size, selector cost, event scheduling, long tasks, framework rerender cost, or
  hydration cost.
- Use `motion-system-contract-review` as an adjunct when UI motion needs state-transition, event,
  timeline-track, interruption, settlement, reduced-motion, channel-collision, role-binding, or
  async-feedback review.
- Use `app-startup-performance-review` as an adjunct when installed app startup needs review from
  icon tap or process launch to first frame and fully usable state, including TTID, TTFD,
  `reportFullyDrawn()`, Application or AppDelegate work, auto-init, DI graph creation, SDK
  initialization, static initializers, main-thread disk or network work, cache snapshots, first
  screen cost, startup profiles, native profilers, React Native imports, Flutter startup, splash
  holds, auth or config gates, and post-first-frame work queues.
- Use `desktop-background-process-stability-review` as an adjunct when Windows services, macOS
  LaunchDaemons or LaunchAgents, Linux systemd units, Electron main or utility processes, WebView
  helpers, tray apps, sync workers, local daemons, auto-start helpers, updaters, desktop background
  jobs, or cross-session desktop processes need crash recovery, durable checkpoints, single-instance
  and data-directory locks, OS-supervisor restart policy, health checks, progress heartbeats, leases,
  idempotent jobs, atomic local writes, shutdown handling, UI and worker lifecycle separation, power
  resume, monotonic time, IPC authorization, deterministic environment, least privilege, early crash
  evidence, update safety, lifecycle tests, or safe mode review.
- Use `desktop-auto-update-safety-review` as an adjunct when installed desktop app update behavior
  needs review for Electron autoUpdater, electron-builder feeds, Squirrel.Windows, Sparkle appcasts,
  Tauri updater, signed and notarized macOS updates, Windows installers, update metadata pointers,
  immutable artifacts, signatures, hash verification, CDN cache policy, staged rollout, deterministic
  canary buckets, alpha/beta/stable channel separation, update kill switches, single-flight update
  checks, quit-and-install timing, old-version upgrade paths, rollback-forward fixes, update
  telemetry, crash gates, or installed-app update smoke tests.
- Use `low-end-device-support-review` as an adjunct when Android Go, low-RAM Android, older iOS,
  React Native, Flutter, Tauri mobile, Electron, desktop app shell, or other constrained-device
  support needs low-end capability budgets across target devices, runtime memory class, cold-start
  frequency, peak memory, image decode, SDK diet, network fan-out, disk writes, cache limits,
  concurrency, UI effects, lists, background work, polling, sensors, and bottom-percentile device
  evidence.
- Use `mobile-energy-efficiency-review` as an adjunct when Android, iOS, React Native, Flutter,
  Tauri mobile, or other mobile app code needs battery and energy review for background work,
  wake locks, exact alarms, Doze, App Standby, push or WebSocket behavior, polling, networking,
  cellular use, location, geofencing, sensors, Bluetooth, rendering, animation, timers, disk I/O,
  Compose recomposition, Low Power Mode, Battery Saver, or platform energy diagnostics.
- Use `frontend-state-ownership-review` as an adjunct when frontend state can drift across props,
  local state, server cache, URL params, form drafts, global stores, context, persisted storage,
  derived selectors, optimistic updates, query keys, request races, or external subscriptions.
- Use `ui-state-resurrection-review` as an adjunct when a closed, completed, cleared, deleted,
  finalized, or dismissed UI surface such as a panel, tab, route, chat stream, draft, task view,
  layout slot, modal, drawer, or notification reappears after reload, restart, reconnect, remount,
  persisted-store hydration, cache restore, replay, migration, crash recovery, cross-tab broadcast,
  cloud sync, or events such as `message.complete`.
- Use `frontend-stress-layout-review` as an adjunct when frontend UI needs hostile-content and
  layout-resilience review for parent container width, container queries, long unbroken strings,
  async media, skeletons, empty, error, permission and loading states, scrollbars, mobile
  viewport or keyboard behavior, safe areas, line clamps, i18n or RTL, touch, reduced motion,
  ResizeObserver, portals, z-index layers, tables, charts, browser zoom, cascade layers, or
  reproducible break conditions.
- Use `frontend-accessibility-tree-review` as an adjunct when frontend accessibility needs
  browser accessibility tree, native HTML semantics, accessible name, visible label, keyboard,
  focus order or return, dialog, form, error, live region, ARIA, hidden content, icon, image alt,
  custom widget, non-text contrast, target size, drag alternative, or automated a11y evidence
  review instead of an "ARIA attributes exist" checklist.
- Use `frontend-component-library-review` as an adjunct when a frontend component library, design
  system package, UI kit, token system, primitive layer, variant API, theming surface, package
  exports, Storybook or docs contract, visual regression suite, codemod, SemVer policy, or
  breaking-change plan needs public API platform review before narrower accessibility, state,
  layout, localization, bundle, or framework skills take over.
- Use `frontend-localization-review` as an adjunct when frontend localization needs all
  user-visible strings, message catalogs, full-sentence translation units, interpolation, plural
  and zero cases, grammar or particles, tone, date/time/number/currency/unit formatting, search,
  sort, Unicode normalization, grapheme-safe truncation, RTL or bidi text, font fallback, pseudo
  localization, SSR locale, fallback, backend error-code mapping, rich text, export, share, or
  notification surface review instead of a visible JSX text scan.
- Use `website-task-friction-review` as an adjunct when a public website, landing page, signup,
  checkout, account, support, navigation, search, form, pricing, consent, or mobile web flow needs
  review for user complaints such as slowness, popups, forced signup, confusing navigation,
  hidden costs, vague errors, dark patterns, weak trust, or missing recovery paths.
- Use `react-code-change` as a primary route when React, React DOM, React Server Components,
  Server Actions, React Compiler, Hooks, Suspense, Actions, forms, refs, context, concurrent
  rendering, SSR streaming, resource hints, package metadata, or React-related tests are created,
  changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `vue-code-change` as a primary route when Vue, Nuxt, Pinia, Vue Router, Vue SFCs,
  Composition API, reactivity, props, emits, slots, `v-model`, SSR, hydration, lazy hydration,
  Vite/Vue toolchain, or Vue-related tests are created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `vite-code-change` as a primary route when Vite config, plugins, Rolldown or Rollup
  compatibility, dependency optimization, dev server or HMR behavior, SSR, library mode, workers,
  Environment API usage, package exports, TypeScript transpilation, browser targets, assets, CSS,
  sourcemaps, package-manager scripts, CI, Docker, preview, or Vite-related tests are created,
  changed, reviewed, migrated, or upgraded.
- Use `babylon-code-change` as a primary route when Babylon.js, WebGPU or WebGL engine setup,
  Scene lifecycle, cameras, lights, meshes, materials, textures, shaders, glTF or GLB loading,
  Havok or Physics V2, LOD, instancing, thin instances, picking, render loops, Inspector
  debugging, or Babylon-related tests are created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `threejs-code-change` as a primary route when Three.js renderer setup, scenes, cameras,
  meshes, materials, textures, shaders, glTF or GLB assets, animation, picking, Raycaster,
  WebGL, WebGPU, WebXR, resource disposal, performance, migration, or related tests change.
- Use `svelte-code-change` as a primary route when Svelte, SvelteKit, route files, universal or
  server load, actions, endpoints, hooks, runes, snippets, bindings, SSR, hydration, streaming,
  invalidation, adapters, Vite, TypeScript, packaging, or Svelte-related tests are created,
  changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `wails-code-change` as a primary route when Wails v3 apps, Go services, generated bindings,
  TypeScript runtime calls, windows, menus, system tray, dialogs, events, WebView platform
  behavior, Taskfile or build config, signing, packaging, platform targets, native desktop CI build
  matrices, custom protocols, file associations, server builds, or Wails-related tests are created,
  changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `axum-code-change` as a primary route when Axum routers, handlers, extractors, state,
  extensions, middleware, Tower or Tower-HTTP layers, CORS, cookies, headers, Tokio tasks or locks,
  SQLx pools, rejections, error responses, body limits, WebSockets, or Rust HTTP API tests are
  created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `nestjs-code-change` as a primary route when NestJS modules, controllers, providers,
  dependency injection, guards, pipes, interceptors, filters, OpenAPI metadata, adapters,
  lifecycle hooks, queues, schedulers, WebSockets, microservices, or Nest-backed HTTP API tests are
  created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `godot-code-change` as a primary route when Godot projects, scenes, nodes, GDScript, C#
  scripts, Resources, Autoloads, signals, groups, save/load systems, rendering, physics, UI,
  input, exports, plugins, editor tools, or Godot version migrations are created, changed, reviewed,
  or upgraded.
- Use `c-code-change` as a primary route when C source, C-owned headers, native C build metadata,
  compiler dialects, C standard-version support, C ABI surfaces, generated C bindings, FFI,
  memory ownership, pointer lifetime, undefined behavior, sanitizer setup, performance-sensitive
  C paths, tests, or benchmarks are created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `shell-code-change` as a primary route when POSIX sh, Bash, shell scripts, shebangs,
  GitHub Actions `run` blocks, package script shell snippets, grep/sed/awk/find/xargs pipelines,
  shell quoting, word splitting, globbing, traps, exit-status handling, or shell
  portability/security behavior are created, changed, reviewed, or upgraded.
- Use `structured-config-change` as a primary route when YAML, TOML, JSON-adjacent config,
  Markdown frontmatter, schema-backed config, or GitHub Actions workflow structure outside shell
  `run` blocks needs parser-dialect, schema, defaulting, normalization, or provider-semantics
  review.
- Use `cache-integrity-review` as an adjunct when cache correctness, key truth, stale data spread,
  invalidation, negative caching, Redis and HTTP cache semantics, permission-cache revocation, or
  cache-outage fallback can mislead users, leak data, or overload source systems.
- Use `security-flow-review` as an adjunct when security review needs source-to-sink tracing across
  authorization, object ownership, tenant scoping, mass assignment, injection inputs, SSRF, files,
  browser rendering, tokens, fail-open behavior, queued work, races, or supply-chain execution.
- Use `input-boundary-validation-review` as an adjunct when untrusted bytes or text cross decoding,
  Unicode canonicalization, duplicate or coercion policy, full parsing, schema, semantic,
  authorization, resource-budget, or structured execution boundaries.
- Use `testability-boundary-review` as an adjunct when review needs to expose hidden decision
  inputs, direct time or randomness, direct I/O, constructor side effects, static or singleton
  state, mock-heavy tests, sleeps, framework magic, reflection-only tests, or other code shapes
  that make important conditions hard to force in tests.
- Use `test-suite-performance-review` as a primary route when test-suite runtime, CI feedback
  latency, selected-test execution, shard balance, worker scheduling, fixture or database setup,
  retry policy, flaky-test handling, result caching, discovery, coverage, or artifact overhead
  needs optimization without weakening verification.
- Use `quadratic-scan-review` as an adjunct when the suspected performance smell is specifically
  hidden O(N^2) work from repeated scans, membership checks, code joins, helper-body lookups,
  render-time lookup, resolver fan-out, repeated sort, or copy accumulation over growing data.
- Use `parser-engineering-review` as an adjunct when lexer, grammar, lossless CST, surface AST or HIR
  lowering, tree visitor, transformer or rewriter behavior, persistent syntax identity, tree
  serialization or compatibility, tree verification, trivia and source origins, operator binding,
  recovery, incremental parsing, Unicode positions, large-input limits, hostile-input budgets, or
  parser fuzzing needs implementation or review.
- Use `fuzz-harness-review` as an adjunct when a coverage-guided target, deterministic reset,
  property or differential oracle, corpus, dictionary, custom mutator, instrumentation or feedback
  mode, stateful sequence, sanitizer lane, exact crash minimization, CI corpus lifecycle, coverage
  plateau, or artifact-triage path needs implementation or review.
- Use `type-state-modeling-review` as an adjunct when code review needs to make impossible
  domain states, invalid ID or unit swaps, nullable/status contradictions, unsafe DTO boundaries,
  or cast-heavy models unrepresentable by type shape.
- Use `race-condition-review` as an adjunct when shared state can be read, yielded, locked,
  retried, published, queued, cancelled, closed, reused, or observed across interleaving execution
  flows.
- Use `async-timing-boundary-review` as an adjunct when arbitrary sleeps, fixed delays, timer
  waits, event-loop yields, render-frame waits, readiness polling, CI waits, Promise completion
  claims, async one-time side effects, or eventual-consistency waits need a real completion signal
  instead of a tuned millisecond value.
- Use `concurrency-invariant-review` as an adjunct when a review needs to prove shared-state
  ownership, whole-invariant protection, lock and condition-variable discipline, memory visibility,
  duplicated execution, shutdown, thread-local context, async interleavings, or deterministic
  concurrency evidence across changed time orders.
- Use `failure-integrity-review` as an adjunct when exception or failure handling can make the
  system lie about success, state, data, money, permissions, locks, queues, logs, metrics, or
  user-visible outcomes.
- Use `backend-log-evidence-review` as an adjunct when backend request, job, worker, scheduler,
  webhook, migration, external API, database write, transaction, state transition, retry, timeout,
  audit, auth, validation, cache, lock, idempotency, feature-flag, release, config, or batch logs
  need review for whether structured events, correlation and causation IDs, outcome/reason fields,
  redaction, sampling, and log schema fields let operators reconstruct why the path reached its
  final state.
- Use `observability-debuggability-review` as an adjunct when logs, metrics, traces, spans,
  dashboards, alerts, runbooks, sampling, redaction, dependency calls, queues, batch jobs, caches,
  pools, rate limits, feature flags, releases, or partial-success paths need review for whether an
  operator can narrow incidents quickly without high-cardinality metric explosions or unsafe
  telemetry data.
- Use `incident-triage-review` as an adjunct when an outage, degradation, timeout spike, p95 or
  p99 latency spike, queue backlog, pool saturation, CPU-idle slowness, OOM, disk or inode pressure,
  DNS or network failure, load balancer 5xx, Kubernetes node or pod issue, deployment regression,
  cache stampede, batch spike, Redis slowdown, DB lock wait, connection leak, conntrack or
  ephemeral-port exhaustion, or log flood needs fast evidence elimination across time, scope,
  change, wait, saturation, dependency, and manual-only diagnostic boundaries.
- Use `deployment-rollout-safety-review` as an adjunct when server, backend, worker, scheduler,
  queue, cron, container, migration, config, feature flag, cache, deployment pipeline, release
  envelope, image digest, deployment history, traffic rollback, canary, rollback, health probe,
  readiness/liveness/startup probe, graceful shutdown, artifact promotion, release observability,
  or post-deploy smoke behavior needs review for whether a deployment can be rolled out, stopped,
  observed, and rolled back safely.
- Use `cloud-cost-guardrail-review` as an adjunct when cloud accounts, projects, subscriptions,
  Kubernetes, serverless, databases, object storage, block storage, snapshots, NAT, public IP,
  egress, CDN, logs, metrics, traces, autoscaling, quotas, budgets, tags, temporary resources,
  container registries, Marketplace, LLM API, or third-party SaaS usage needs review for whether
  spend can silently explode without account isolation, caps, lifecycle, retention, attribution,
  or automated non-production stop guardrails. For CI runner-minute, workflow matrix, artifact
  retention, cache quota, or release-asset handoff cost, use `ci-pipeline-triage` first.
- Use `rate-limit-integrity-review` as an adjunct when rate limits, throttling, quotas, API usage
  limits, request costs, token buckets, fixed or sliding windows, GCRA, Redis counters, edge,
  gateway, service, tenant, user, API key, route-group, IP, 429, `Retry-After`, `RateLimit`,
  shadow mode, operator reset, async enqueue, cached-hit counting, or concurrency-limit overlap
  need review for protected-resource fit, key design, atomic counting, layered enforcement, and
  client contract.
- Use `idempotency-integrity-review` as an adjunct when repeated requests, retries, webhooks,
  queue redelivery, schedulers, batch replays, double clicks, provider callbacks, timeout
  recovery, or duplicate business commands can make the same logical operation move state or
  external side effects more than once.
- Use `retry-policy-integrity-review` as an adjunct when retry loops, SDK or client retry configs,
  backoff, jitter, timeout, deadline, `Retry-After`, retry predicates, layered retries, circuit
  breakers, bulkheads, token buckets, queue redelivery, broker retries, cancellation-aware sleeps,
  prompt repair, model or tool fallback, replanning, repeated failure signatures, self-correction,
  or retry observability can amplify failures, duplicate side effects, hide permanent errors,
  exhaust pools, or overload dependencies.
- Use `queue-processing-integrity-review` as an adjunct when queues, streams, pub/sub handlers,
  workers, task runners, consumers, producers, ack, delete, offset commit, visibility timeout,
  publisher confirm, prefetch, rebalance, DLQ, redelivery, or worker-loss behavior can lose work,
  duplicate work, hide poison messages, reorder state, exhaust consumers, or falsely claim
  processing success.
- Use `transaction-boundary-integrity-review` as an adjunct when transactions, ORM atomic blocks,
  unit-of-work code, database write paths, framework transaction annotations, isolation levels,
  locks, retries, after-commit side effects, outbox patterns, or transactional tests need review
  for read-decision-write integrity rather than only query speed, generic races, or failure prose.
- Use `database-query-bottleneck-review` as an adjunct when database review needs to catch query
  bottlenecks from cardinality explosion, N+1 access, overfetching, unstable pagination,
  index-defeating predicates, plan skew, or long transaction scope before live plan evidence.
- Use `search-index-integrity-review` as a primary route when keyword search, full-text search,
  Elasticsearch, OpenSearch, Lucene-style indexing, aliases, bulk ingestion, refresh visibility,
  analyzer, metadata taxonomy, negative metadata, exact keyword fields, source maps, synonym,
  autocomplete, pagination, shard failure, search quality, or search performance needs
  source-to-search and query-contract evidence.
- Use `vector-search-integrity-review` as a primary route when vector search, semantic search, RAG
  retrieval, embeddings, contextual headers, synthetic questions, chunk text variants, ANN indexes,
  exact-versus-approximate search, filters, metadata, namespaces, tenants, hybrid search, reranking,
  recall, latency, or golden-set behavior needs retrieval-contract review.
- Use `rag-pipeline-triage` as a primary route when a RAG, knowledge-base answer, grounded chat,
  citation answer, document QA, or support bot failure is not yet localized to ingestion, parsing,
  document metadata, frontmatter schema, source maps, heading paths, chunking, retrieval, filtering,
  reranking, context assembly, prompt construction, generation, citation validation, answerability,
  access control, latency, or cost.
- Use `database-json-modeling-review` as an adjunct when database review needs to decide whether
  JSON, jsonb, metadata, settings, raw payload, or dynamic keys should become typed columns,
  child tables, generated/computed columns, JSON indexes, schema versions, or key registries
  instead of being treated as schema-free storage.
- Use `deletion-lifecycle-review` as an adjunct when data deletion, restore, retention, legal hold,
  purge, tombstone, backup residue, downstream deletion, or tenant offboarding needs lifecycle
  review rather than a single `DELETE`, `is_deleted`, or `deleted_at` check.
- Use `database-lock-contention-review` as an adjunct when database review needs to catch hot rows,
  lock waits, deadlocks, over-strong row locks, gap or metadata locks, queue claim contention,
  chunking, timeout policy, pool waits, or lock observability rather than only query speed.
- Use `command-intent-mapping-gate` when outside text, docs, AI output, snippets, or reports suggest
  commands before running, preserving, or documenting those commands.
- Use `public-json-contract-change` instead of the broader CLI-output route when JSON, JSONL,
  schema-backed reports, stream routing, fixtures, or exit-code semantics are the public contract.
- Use `template-install-surface-sync` instead of the broader contract-sync route when a change
  affects installed template files, manifest `creates`, skill profiles, locale policy, or init/update
  behavior.
- Use `runtime-target-selection` before language-specific skills when the task chooses, migrates,
  rewrites, or justifies a primary language, runtime, compile target, framework, or execution
  environment. After a target is selected, apply the matching language-specific skill before code
  edits in that target.
- Use `structure-first-engineering` as an adjunct for non-trivial implementation work when domain
  rules, public contracts, external I/O, operational safety, failure handling, concurrency,
  data flow, or future change cost could be shaped by early structure decisions. Do not use it for
  surface-only changes or tiny local edits with no boundary pressure.
- Use `support-surface-advisor` as a primary route before building a product, app, service, CLI,
  API, SDK, library, desktop app, automation tool, or developer tool when the agent must decide
  which user, developer, operator, automation, integration, recovery, upgrade, or observability
  routes are supported now, deferred, or explicitly not supported.
- Use `secret-exposure-response` as an event route when a real or plausible secret value appears;
  do not treat redaction as proof that rotation, revocation, or history exposure is handled.
- Use `evidence-stall-breaker` as an event route when the same read, list, search, path, or review
  observation repeats without new evidence, a duplicate-call guard appears, or an agent is about to
  make a confident repository claim from stale, failed, truncated, or missing evidence.
- Treat event-triggered skills as inactive until the event occurs. For example, read
  `failure-triage` only after a configured command intent or verification step fails.
- If several main routes appear to match, choose the one tied to the files and behavior being
  changed now, then report the skipped plausible routes instead of reading every route.

## Classification Prefilter

Use this table only to reduce the first-pass skill categories. The route category gate below remains
the source for the first routing step.

| Classification evidence | First-pass skill category |
| --- | --- |
| `docs_change`, `copy_change`, `i18n_change`, `release_risk` | Documentation and Release |
| `test_change`, `test_policy_change`, `behavior_change` | Tests and Regression |
| `code_change`, `public_api_change`, `unknown_change` | General Code Change, then Architecture Patterns only when structural pressure is concrete |
| `mustflow_docs_change`, `mustflow_config_change` | Workflow and Contract Maintenance |
| Security, privacy, data, or external-system paths | Security and Privacy, or Data and External Systems |

## Route Category Gate

Choose one first-pass category before scanning specific routes. This keeps routine docs, bug, and
test tasks from requiring a full read of architecture-pattern routes. Categories are backed by
`.mustflow/skills/routes.toml`; keep that metadata aligned with the tables below.

| Category | Use When | Next Step |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Bug and Failure | Failures, regressions, confusing behavior, or command failures. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| General Code Change | Orientation, implementation, review, and ordinary code-change risk. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Tests and Regression | Test design, maintenance, TDD, and requirement coverage. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Documentation and Release | Documentation, release wording, source freshness, and prose review. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Security and Privacy | Secrets, personal data, external prompt text, and security regression risk. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Data and External Systems | Persistence, adapters, dependency boundaries, migrations, and external systems. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| UI and Assets | UI surfaces, review artifacts, package artifacts, and web assets. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Architecture Patterns | Pattern-specific routes; use only after concrete structural pressure appears. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |
| Workflow and Contract Maintenance | mustflow workflow, routes, context, contracts, coordination, and metadata. | Inspect only this category's specific route table first; add adjunct or event routes only when their trigger appears. |

## Specific Routes

After choosing a category, choose one main route (`primary` or `authoring`) and at most two adjunct
routes. Event routes stay inactive until their event occurs.

### Bug and Failure

| Trigger | Skill Document | Required Input | Edit Scope | Risk | Verification Intents | Expected Output |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| A configured command intent or verification step fails | `.mustflow/skills/failure-triage/SKILL.md` | Failing intent and output tail | Failure cause only | misdiagnosis | `mustflow_check`; original failing intent | Root cause, fix, rerun result |
| Code review, debugging, failure triage, security review, or repeated review produces a candidate defect claim that needs evidence gating, semantic deduplication, scope and regression classification, closure, or a bounded stop decision | `.mustflow/skills/bug-claim-evidence-gate/SKILL.md` | Candidate trigger, allowed and actual results, current revision and scope, applicable obligation, witness or evidence gap, existing finding state, and configured command intents | Prefer read-only adjudication; update only an explicitly configured finding ledger, never application code, canonical tests, oracle policy, receipts, or prior ledger events | failing-test-as-bug collapse, invented oracle, regression inflation, stale evidence, scope laundering, duplicate wording, one-pass flaky closure, endless review, or false clean result | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `test_related`, `test_audit`, `mustflow_check` | Frozen envelope, classification axes, obligation, witness and gaps, canonical finding or rejection, duplicate or closure decision, stop state, routing, verification, and remaining risk |
| The same read, list, search, path, or review observation repeats without new evidence; a duplicate-call guard appears; or a review/completion claim would rely on stale, failed, truncated, directory-only, or missing evidence | `.mustflow/skills/evidence-stall-breaker/SKILL.md` | Repeated tool call signature, prior result or warning, claim at risk, inspected sources, and next different observation strategy | Investigation path, review wording, completion evidence, and the smallest in-scope skill or workflow wording when preserving the failure mode | hallucinated codebase claim, fake review finding, exhausted tool budget, or false completion | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `mustflow_check` | Stalled observation, evidence ledger, changed strategy or stopped branch, downgraded claims, verification, and remaining evidence gaps |
| A bug or confusing failure needs a fix before the smallest deterministic reproduction or cause is clear | `.mustflow/skills/repro-first-debug/SKILL.md` | Symptom, expected behavior, observed output, failing intent or action, likely changed files, and known flakiness or environment limits | Diagnostic reads, focused reproduction, temporary instrumentation, smallest fix, and symptom-tied regression guard | speculative fix, flaky reproduction, lingering debug output, broad unrelated test, or over-testing | `test_related`, `test_fast`, `mustflow_check` | Symptom, reproduction path or gap, hypotheses, observations, fix, original reproduction rerun, verification, and remaining risk |
| Reported API, SDK, browser, mobile, webhook, gateway, CDN, load balancer, provider, wrong-status, wrong-body, CORS preflight, auth, rate-limit, cache, OpenAPI, or deployment-config failure is not yet localized to the client, network, proxy, app, database, cache, provider, or deployment boundary | `.mustflow/skills/api-failure-triage/SKILL.md` | Failing request packet, success comparator, boundary ledger, timing ledger, contract ledger, auth ledger, change ledger, redaction constraints, and configured command intents | Request/response evidence preservation, success/failure wire comparison, boundary localization, timing decomposition, status/body/content-type mapping, CORS/preflight split, redirect and proxy header checks, authn/authz split, retry/timeout/rate-limit/idempotency classification, cache and OpenAPI drift checks, focused reproduction fixtures, and directly synchronized docs or templates | log-first debugging, SDK argument theater, missing failing packet, success-only comparison, CORS blamed for server-to-server calls, redirect losing auth or method, proxy stripping idempotency or trace headers, `200` error body, HTML body with JSON content type, authn/authz collapse, object-auth incident missed, clock-skew flake, retry storm, non-idempotent replay, 429 hidden as 500, stale CDN or browser cache, OpenAPI drift, deployment config drift, or unfalsifiable log reading | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `lint`, `build`, `test_related`, `test`, `docs_validate_fast`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | API failure triaged, request packet and comparator, boundary and timing ledger, localized cause or evidence gap, hypotheses killed or open, fix or recommendation, evidence level, verification, and remaining API-failure risk |
| Login, signup, logout, refresh, password reset, magic link, passkey, MFA, OAuth, OIDC, JWT, cookie, session, token exchange, provider callback, account-linking, or authorization-after-login behavior is failing or intermittent before the failing identity boundary is known | `.mustflow/skills/auth-flow-triage/SKILL.md` | Auth attempt packet, stage ledger, token and session ledger, browser and proxy ledger, provider ledger, denial and privacy ledger, redaction constraints, and configured command intents | Auth stage localization, sanitized success/failure comparison, cookie and CORS credential checks, proxy trust and redirect URI checks, state, nonce, PKCE, issuer and subject checks, token and JWKS validation, session refresh and logout checks, passkey and MFA checks, account-linking checks, focused denial tests, and directly synchronized docs or templates | login-as-one-bucket debugging, token or cookie logging, account enumeration, loose redirect matching, state or nonce bypass, PKCE mismatch hidden, issuer plus subject ignored, SameSite or Secure drift, forwarded-header trust bug, refresh-token race, session fixation, email-only account linking, stale token claims, clock-skew flake, broad CORS wildcard, or unverified provider-console assumption | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `lint`, `build`, `test_related`, `test`, `test_audit`, `docs_validate_fast`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | Auth flow triaged, failing stage and comparator, cookie/proxy/provider/token/session/passkey/MFA findings, fix or recommendation, evidence level, verification, and remaining auth-flow risk |
| Docker Engine, Docker Desktop, daemon, context, Compose, container start, crash loop, health check, image pull, build cache, port mapping, DNS, network, volume, bind mount, storage, proxy, registry, cgroup, OOM, signal handling, PID 1, or runtime behavior is failing before the failing container boundary is known | `.mustflow/skills/docker-runtime-triage/SKILL.md` | Runtime packet, container ledger, actual config ledger, host resource ledger, network ledger, storage ledger, evidence-preservation constraints, and configured command intents | Host, daemon, context, image, container, Compose, process, resource, storage, network, proxy, registry, and build boundary localization; evidence preservation before cleanup; focused Dockerfile, Compose, health, entrypoint, network, volume, resource, docs, fixture, or test edits only after localization | prune-before-evidence, restart loop hiding first error, app blame before daemon proof, logs-only diagnosis, exit code 137 treated as automatic OOM, PID 1 signal loss, container localhost confusion, bind mount hiding image files, Compose variable drift, tag identity confusion, stale build cache, broad firewall reset, volume deletion, or unbounded raw Docker command | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `lint`, `build`, `test_related`, `test`, `docs_validate_fast`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | Docker runtime triaged, boundary findings, evidence preserved and missing, fix or recommendation, evidence level, verification, and remaining Docker runtime risk |
| CI/CD workflow, pipeline, job, matrix, trigger, required check, runner, cache, artifact, runner-minute billing, artifact storage or retention, deployment step, or post-deploy verification is failing, skipped, queued, flaky, slow, unexpectedly expensive, or green despite broken output before the failing or expensive pipeline boundary is known | `.mustflow/skills/ci-pipeline-triage/SKILL.md` | Failure classification, run identity ledger, last-good comparison, CI billing ledger when cost is in scope, boundary ledger, redaction constraints, and configured command intents | Trigger, parsed graph, queue, runner, environment, dependency, build, test, cache, artifact, billing, deploy, smoke, and final status localization; false-green checks; runner-minute and storage-quota separation; safe diagnostic evidence; focused workflow, package, docs, fixture, or test edits only after localization | last-red-line debugging, latest-code comparison, rerun-green treated as fixed, skipped required check, path-filter pending state, hidden `continue-on-error`, queue time mistaken for build time, runner-minute billing mistaken for artifact storage, plan allowance unit confusion, matrix split rounding loss, premium runner surprise, floating `latest`, secret logging, sleep-based service readiness, cache-as-artifact confusion, deploying untested rebuilt artifacts, fork token scope surprise, unguarded environment concurrency, or zero-exit deploy without smoke evidence | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `lint`, `build`, `test_related`, `test`, `docs_validate_fast`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | CI pipeline triaged, failure or cost shape and localized boundary, run identity and last-good comparison, trigger/runner/environment/build/test/cache/artifact/billing/deploy/verification findings, verification, and remaining CI pipeline risk |

### General Code Change

| Trigger | Skill Document | Required Input | Edit Scope | Risk | Verification Intents | Expected Output |

### Tests and Regression

| Trigger | Skill Document | Required Input | Edit Scope | Risk | Verification Intents | Expected Output |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| User requirements, acceptance criteria, issue reports, bug reports, product notes, compatibility promises, or examples must be preserved as regression coverage before or during implementation | `.mustflow/skills/requirement-regression-guard/SKILL.md` | Requirement source, observable behavior, existing tests or fixtures, implementation scope, changed files, and command contract entries | Focused tests, fixtures, examples, schemas, docs, and implementation changes directly tied to the requirement | untested requirement, invented acceptance criteria, weakened tests, hidden behavior drift, or unverifiable implementation claim | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `test_related`, `test`, `test_audit`, `docs_validate_fast`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | Requirement sources, coverage map, guards added or reused, implementation changes, deferred requirements, verification, and remaining regression risk |
| The user explicitly requests TDD, test-first work, red-green-refactor, RED/GREEN, or one observable behavior slice at a time | `.mustflow/skills/vertical-slice-tdd/SKILL.md` | TDD trigger, first behavior contract, existing tests, expected RED category, baseline status, and command contract entries | One focused test or fixture, the smallest implementation for the current slice, and directly synchronized docs when needed | invalid RED, broad slice, premature refactor, unrelated cleanup, or verification claim without configured command evidence | `changes_status`, `changes_diff_summary`, `test_related`, `test_audit`, `test`, `lint`, `build`, `mustflow_check` | Slice scope, existing coverage, RED category evidence, GREEN verification, refactors after GREEN, deferred slices, and remaining TDD risk |
| New tests or test cases are designed, TDD RED or GREEN evidence is reported, or test-case choices are made for requirements, bugs, refactors, security boundaries, schemas, templates, or public docs | `.mustflow/skills/test-design-guard/SKILL.md` | Contract source, existing coverage, intended RED evidence, candidate cases, baseline status, and command contract entries | Tests, fixtures, helpers, and directly synchronized contract docs | invalid RED, happy-path-only coverage, speculative edge cases, weak assertions, mock-only confidence, or implementation-detail coupling | `test_related`, `test_audit`, `test`, `lint`, `build`, `test_release`, `mustflow_check` | RED category, selected test shape, evidence-backed cases, rejected speculation, verification objective, commands, and remaining test-design risk |
| A coverage-guided fuzz target, persistent harness, property-based generator integration, differential or metamorphic oracle, corpus, dictionary, custom mutator, sanitizer lane, instrumentation or feedback setup, stateful campaign, crash minimization, CI corpus lifecycle, coverage plateau, non-reproducible artifact, or fuzzing-effectiveness claim is created, changed, reviewed, debugged, or reported | `.mustflow/skills/fuzz-harness-review/SKILL.md` | Target and stage matrix, deterministic entropy and reset model, semantic result envelope, property and divergence identifiers, oracle and
